## Raise Dead Fully

> **Raise Dead Fully**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 14 **R:** near (~18 m / 60 ft)  
> **T:** one dead creature body (full human/demihuman recovery; broader living creatures by stricter limits) **D:** permanent
>
> You perform high-tier full resurrection. Human and demihuman recipients return immediately at full Life and normal function, retaining pre-death afflictions unless separately cured.
>
> For non-human/demihuman living creatures, harsher Raise Dead-style limits apply.
>
> Anti-undead clause: destroys weaker undead outright, heavily pressures mid-tier undead saves, and deals heavy damage to stronger undead.
>
> _Reverse — Obliterate:_ Inverts the effect for lethal anti-living application and restorative anti-undead inversion behavior by doctrine.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:other]
>   [storage:item]
>   [resurrection]
>   [undead]
>   [high-tier]
>   [reversible]

meta:
> - source:
>   - becmi:Companion Set; spell: Raise Dead Fully
>   - becmi:Master Set; spell: Raise Dead Fully
>   - becmi:Rules Cyclopedia; spell: Raise Dead Fully
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Raise Dead Fully; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

osr:
[Companion | High-Level Cleric, Druid, and Magic-User Spell Material -> Seventh-Level Cleric Spells]
3. Raise Dead Fully*

[Master | Seventh-Level Cleric Spells]
      raise dead fully
   3. Ability score penalty: The user loses 6-
       11 (id6 +5) points of Strength, to a
      minimum Strength of 3.
   Source: Norse mythology
   Further Research: See standard works,
referring to the following names. Verthandi is
one of the Norns of Norse legend, the immor-
tal beings who rule the fates of men and gods
alike. Verthandi rules the Present, Urdur (or
Urdhr, or Urth) the Past, and Skuld (who
wears a veil), the Future. Each of the Norns
may provide ideas for other artifacts.
   Your Notes:

WIFE OF ILMARINEN
 The legendary Immortal craftsman
 Ilmarinen once used his great skills to cre-
 ate a companion entirely of gold and silver.
 However, the result was too cold to even be
 approached. Appearing as a metallic
 golem, it was given special powers when
 freed, and is said to reside in far northern
 reaches, either alone or with its current
 master.

  Description: The wife appears to be a
metal statue of an extremely attractive
human female clad in robes. The entire
statue is made of a sparkling mixture of gold
and silver.
   Magnitude: Minor artifact.
   Power Limits: 2/A, 1/B, 2/C, 3/D
   Sphere: Matter (Fighters, earth)
   Suggested Powers (PP 100):
A1     Ice breath                       55
A1     Ice storm                        45
   Activation: The wife is always active.
   Use of Powers: The powers of the wife are
used by the artifact alone, not granted to the
user. The wife can speak any language it
hears, and will explain its powers to any who
ask (unless ordered not to). However, the
artifact cannot be controlled until a special
command word is uttered. Once this com-
mand is spoken, the wife will obey either
mental or verbal commands from the user.
The command word can only be obtained
from Ilmarinen himself (by using a com-
mune or contact other plane), from a pre-
vious user of the artifact, or by a wish.
   Suggested Handicap (1): When control is
gained, the user becomes aware that the wife
cannot recharge itself. It can eat gold or sil-
ver. For each 100 gp value of those metals
eaten, the artifact recharges 1 PP.
   Suggested Penalty (1; 1 in 6 chance of
occurrence whenever a power is used): In-
stead of attacking as directed, the wife aims
her attack at the user; normal saving throws
apply, but the user gains a +4 bonus for the
second and subsequent appearances of this
effect.
   Other Details: AC -20; hp 100; AT 1
power; D by power; M V 90' (30'); AL N.
The wife will not attack by any means other
than its powers.
   Source: Finnish mythology
   Further Research: See the Finnish
national epic poem Kalevala, compiled by
 Elias Lonnrott in the late 19th century.
   Your Notes:

The following legendary magic items are
mentioned in history, myths, legends, and lit-
erature. You may easily develop them into
either artifacts or powerful but standard
magic items. Further research is recom-
mended.

   Ambrosia: This is a potion of Immortality,
but with a short duration. Repeated drinks
are needed to maintain Immortal status.
   Apples of Bragi: In Scandinavian legend,
Bragi (son of Odin) had a magically inex-
haustible supply of these items. Each can
cure weariness, decay of power, ill temper, or
failing health.
   Arrow of Abaris: Abaris the Hyperbo-
rean, a Greek sage in the 6th century BC,
once received a magic arrow from the god
Apollo (according to Greek legend). The
arrow enabled him to become invisible, cure
disease, fly (riding the arrow, as if a broom)
and to divine the future.
    Bag of Aeolus: In Homer's Odyssey, this
bag (named for the god of winds) contains a
divine essence. When opened, it blows Odys-
seus' ship back to its starting point.
    Books, Sibylline: These were written
prophecies, carefully preserved in ancient
Rome and occasionally consulted on matters
of great import. There were nine scrolls at
first, offered for sale to Rome by the seeress
Almathaea; the Romans refused her price.
She kept to the price and burned 3, but again
was turned down. She sold the remaining 3 at
the original price. They were preserved in a
stone chest, with two custodians (later
increased to 10 and then 15). Finally placed
in gilt cases at the base of the statue of Apollo
on Palatine Hill, they were burned in the
great fire of Nero's fame.
    Carpet, Solomon's Magic: This item,
made of green silk, was legended to have car-
ried not only Solomon and his great throne
but also all of his army.
    Draupnir: In Scandinavian legend, the
 famed magic ring made by Odin (the
 supreme deity) for the dwarves. Every 9
 nights it produced 8 non-magical rings equal
 in size and beauty to itself, and is thus a fertil-
 ity symbol.
    Elixir: In Arabic legend, this powder was
 sprinkled on wounds of battle, curing them.
 Treat as a potion of healing, but applied
 instead of consumed.
    Holy Grail: This vessel of literary fame
 was the cup at the Last Supper, carried to
 England by Joseph of Arimathea. It was said
 to provide food, drink, and spiritual suste-
 nance for the life of the custodian. This term
 may have originally been used in reference to
 the platter of the Paschal lamb (again, at the
 Last Supper).
    Horse, flying: Clavileno, an enchanted
 wooden rocking horse described in Cer-
 vantes' "Don Quixote," could fly and carry
 an armed rider. It was guided by a pin in its
 forehead.

    Mill: A magic mill in the Finnish
 "Kalevala," called the Sampo, could grind
out meal, salt, or gold from straw on com-
mand.
   Necklace of Harmonia: Harmonia,
daughter of the Greek gods Ares and Aphro-
dite, was given a magical necklace when she
married Cadmus. Though relatively unre-
markable at the time, the necklace brought
disaster to all subsequent owners.
   Odrovir: In Norse legend, a great war
took place between the Aesir (the 24 gods of
heaven, Asgard) and the Vanir (the Nature
gods of Noatun). At its peaceful conclusion,
both sides spat into a jar, providing their
mixed essences as hostage to peace. Kvasir,
the wisest of all men, was made of the spittle.
His blood, mixed with honey, was called
Odrovir (or Odhrevir); all who partook of it
became poets.
   Ring of Amasis: Amasis, King of Egypt,
advised his incredibly lucky friend Polycra-
tes, King of Samos, to discard something of
great value to balance the Fates. Polycrates
threw a prized ring into the sea, but it was
later found in a fish on the King's dinner
table. Amasis promptly recognized this sign
from the gods and broke off relations with his
friend; shortly thereafter, Polycrates was bru-
tally slain.
   Ring of the Nibelungen: Made famous by
Richard Wagner's 1876 opera, this item
comes from several Scandinavian legends
(the Volsunga Saga, Nibelungenlied, Elder
and Younger Eddas, and the Eckelied). The
ring was part of an entire hoard in the Rhine
river, which was guarded by the Rhine Maid-
ens until Alberich gained it by foreswearing
love. The greedy dwarf cursed the item, and
when the Ring was later taken by gods and
heroes for various uses, it brought doom to
all, resulting even in the destruction of
Asgard and the gods.
   Swords: Many magical swords can be
found in myth and literature. The following
list is only a sampling; further research is rec-
ommended to ascertain appropriate powers.
   Angurvadal (Stream of Anguish) was
owned by the hero of "Frithiofs Saga," a
13th century Scandinavian work.
   Ar'ondight, sword of Launcelot of the
Lake, was mentioned in several Arthurian
legends.
   Balisarda (a sword of slicing) was made by
the witch Falerina in the 1487 romance epic
"Orlando Innamorato" (Roland in Love) by
Matteo Maria Boiardo.
   Balmung was the sword of Siegfried in
Scandinavian legend. It was made by
Wieland, a Germanic name for the immortal

blacksmith Volund, known as "Wayland
Smith" to the English. (See the artifact
Armet by Wayland.) Wieland may be similar
to earlier legends, such as the Greek
Hephaestus and the Roman Vulcan.
   Colada was the sword of the Spanish hero
El Cid, first described in a poem of a
unknown Castilian bard in 1140. "Cid"
comes from the Arabic "Sidi," or "Lord."
The hero was Ruy Diaz de Bivar (1043-
 1099), also called "ed Campeador" (the
Champion).
   Courtain ("the Short Sword") was used by
Ogier the Dane, a Paladin of Charlemagne
(who, known as Holger Danske, is the folk
hero of Denmark). The smith Munifican
took 3 years to make Courtain.
   Durandan (or Durandal, Durandana, or
"the Inflexible") was the Sword of Roland,
given him by Charlemagne. It once belonged
to Hector, the noble chieftain of Homer's
"Iliad" prominent in the fall of Troy. Roland
(also called Orlando) is the hero of several lit-
erary works, including the "Chanson de
Roland" (Song of Roland) of the 11th cen-
tury; the "Chronicle of Charlemagne" of the
12th century; and the later Italian works
"Morgante Maggiore" by Luigi Pulci
(1 483), Boiardo's "Orlando Innamorato"
(Roland in Love, 1487), and "Orlando Furi-
oso" (Roland Mad, 1516) by Lodovico
Ariosto.
   Excalibur(or Escalibor, in the Old French)
was the fabled sword of King Arthur (accord-
ing to most legends). It was also referred to as
Caliburn (by Geoffrey of Monmouth) and
Caledvwlch (in the Mabinogion), or Calad-
bolg in Irish legend (meaning "hard belly").
It gets its name from the Latin "ex calce
liberare," or "to liberate from the stone."
   Flarnberge (or Floberge, meaning Flame
Cutter) was a sword of Charlemagne.
   Glorius, sword of the hero Oliver, broke 9
swords made by the famed smiths Ansias,
Galas, and Munifican.
   Gram (German for "grief') was another
famous sword of Siegfried.
  Joyeuse (French, "joyous"), a greatsword
of Charlemagne, took 3 years to make (by the
smith Gallas).
   Mimung, sword of the hero Wittich, was
loaned to Siegfried for a time.
   Morglay (Big Glaive) was the sword of Sir
Bevis of English lore. "Morglay" was then a
common generic term for "sword."
   Nagelring (Nail-Ring) was the sword of
Dietrich of Bern, a hero in the Germanic
"Heldenbuch" and "Nibelungenlied."
   Philippan was the sword of Mark Antony,
a member of the Second Triumvirate of

Rome (43 BC).
   Sauvagine was another of Ogier's swords
(see "Courtain"), also made by Munifican.


[Rules Cyclopedia | Clerical Spells List and Spell Descriptions]
Raise Dead Fully*
Range: 60'
Duration: Permanent
Effect: Raises any living creature
This spell is similar to the 5th level spell raise
dead, except that it can raise any living
creature—not just humans and demihumans.
Any human or demihuman recipient awakens
immediately, with full hit points, and is able to
fight, use abilities, spells known, etc., without
any penalties—except those penalties the crea-
ture already possessed at the time of death. For
example, a victim cursed or diseased at death
would still suffer the affliction when raised fully.
If any other living creature (other than a hu-
man or demihuman) is the recipient, the guide-
lines given in the raise dead spell apply
(including time limitations, rest needed, etc.).
A 17th level cleric can use this spell on a hu-
man or demihuman body that has been dead up
to 4 months; for each level of experience above
17th, this time increases 4 months. Thus, a 19th
level cleric could cast raise dead fully on a body
that has been dead up to 12 months.
The spell is fatal to undead. Cast on an un-
dead creature of 7 Hit Dice or less, the spell im-
mediately destroys the creature (no saving
throw). The spell forces an undead creature of 7
to 12 Hit Dice to make a saving throw vs. spells,
with a - 4 penalty to the roll; if the creature fails
the roll, it is destroyed. The spell inflicts 6d10
(6-60) points of damage upon an undead mon-
ster of more than 12 Hit Dice, but the victim
may make a saving throw vs. spells to take half
damage.
The reverse of this spell (obliterate) will affect
a living creature just as the normal form affects
undead (destroy 7 Hit Dice or less, et al.). If cast
at an undead creature of any type, obliterate has
the same effect as a cureall would on a living
creature (curing all but 1d6 points of damage, or
curing blindness or feeblemind, etc.).

## Animate Dead

> **Animate Dead**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 6 **R:** near (~18 m / 60 ft)  
> **T:** one or more intact corpses or skeletal remains **D:** permanent until destroyed or released
>
> You call corpse-matter into a hostile motion state, raising skeletons or zombies under your command. Raised undead follow direct orders and defend themselves if uncontrolled, but they are mindless and interpret commands literally.
>
> You may control total undead Hit Dice up to roughly twice your Level through this power; beyond that, older creations go feral, dormant, or hostile at referee call.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 - raise one additional corpse in the same activation; x4 - grant raised undead a brief coordinated action burst on the round they rise.
>
> See also: `Animate Corpse` in the SDM Powers Index for a close descendant variant.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:other]
>   [storage:item]
>   [necromancy]
>   [summon]
>   [control]
>   [dangerous]

osr:
[Expert | Clerical and Magic-User Spell Expansions]
Animate Dead
Range: 60'
Duration: Permanent
Effect: Creates zombies or skeletons
This spell allows the caster to make ani-
mated, enchanted skeletons or zombies
from normal skeletons or dead bodies
within range. These animated undead
creatures will obey the cleric until they are
destroyed by another cleric or a dispel magic
spell. For each level of the cleric, one Hit
Die of undead may be animated. A skel-
eton has the same Hit Dice as the original
creature, but a zombie has one Hit Die
more than the original. Character levels
are not counted (the remains of a 9th level
thief would be animated as a zombie with 2
HD). Animated creatures do not have any
spells, but are immune to sleep and charm
effects and poison.
lawful clerics must take care to use this
spell only for good purpose. Animating
the dead is usually a Chaotic act.

[Rules Cyclopedia | Clerical and Magical Spells Lists and Spell Descriptions]
Animate Dead
Range: 60'
Duration: Permanent
Effect: Creates zombies or skeletons
This spell allows the spellcaster to make ani-
mated, enchanted skeletons or zombies from
normal skeletons or dead bodies within range.
These animated undead creatures will obey the
cleric until they are destroyed by another cleric or
a dispel magic spell.
For each experience level of the cleric, he may
animate one Hit Die of undead. A skeleton has
the same Hit Dice as the original creature, but a
zombie has one Hit Die more than the original.
Note that this doesn't count character experi-
ence levels as Hit Dice: For purposes of this spell,
all humans and demihumans are 1 HD crea-
tures, so the remains of a 9th level thief would
be animated as a zombie with 2 HD.
Animated creatures do not have any spells.
but are immune to sleep and charm effects and
poison. Lawful clerics must take care to use this
spell only for good purpose. Animating the dead
is usually a Chaotic act.

# Heritage Powers

These magitech (oldtech) and sorcery (fantascience) Powers are practiced by the fae tribes and clans of Elyncia. If tagged with a Heritage, characters with good factional standing can purchase them at a 50% discount from friendly factions that practice these Powers.

Heritage-origin recognizers now indexed under OSR sections: `Swamp’s Gift (Water Breathing)` in Traversal and Mobility, and `Veilwalk (Passwall)` in Dimensional, Planar, and Exotic Access.

Avatar of the Dream, Summon Guardian Spirit, Breath Weapon, Dream Pounce, Enchanting Melody, Elemental Gift, Psychedelic Veil, Shadowform, Laughing Curse, Echo Memory, Prey-Binder, and Flow-Arts — katas and jurus codified as balance, strike, and footwork forms taught from youth.

All spider folk clans share three heritage powers (Level 1 rites): **Cast Web** (craft snares or silk resources), **Leap** (double jump distance for a scene), **Swarm Sense** (summon swarm creature once per watch).

**Swarm Sense** – Once per watch, you may call or dismiss rodents (rats, mice, squirrels) within Level \+ Thought × 10 yd.

* They gather to provide **advantage on Recon or Salvage rolls** for 1 day.

* If these rolls botch (natural 1) they scatter or panic — you must make an Aura Save to avoid being nipped, harried, or fatigued.

 Master (choose at the moment you trigger it, once/scene):  
 *Stampede*: Rush up to your Speed through enemies; each must Save or be shoved 1 square and shaken (–1) for a round.  
 *Brush Phantom*: Immediately Hide (even in light cover) and Dash (move up to Speed without provoking reactions); your next attack from hiding has Advantage.

Grave-Wrought Gift, Crown of the Grave, Soul Anchor

## Assimilation Protocol

> **Assimilation Protocol**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 8 **R:** self  
> **T:** self **D:** instant
>
> Heritages: Awakened Vome
>
>
>
> Once per watch, initiate a link handshake with a machine, construct, vome, or cybernetic organism within (Level \+ Thought) × 10 yd. The target must choose:
>
> * **Accept** — You both gain \+1 to all rolls involving each other for the next watch and may share Power points freely while within sight of each other.
> * **Refuse** — Target makes an **Attrition (Wear & Tear) Save**. On a fail, they lose 1 Endurance or Aura. If they cannot lose Endurance or Aura, they suffer Wear and Tear instead: maximum Life is reduced by Level, and the wear occupies a Burden slot until removed.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — standard escalation per referee call.

>   [storage:burden]

>   [vome]
>   [stance]

## Avatar of the Dream

> **Avatar of the Dream**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 6 **R:** Self; effects extend to nearby nodes/glyphs in the local Nexus  
> **T:** Self; plus up to (Level) nearby allies for linked actions **D:** One scene, or until ended as noted below
>
> Once per watch, root your psychic self into the local Noösphere as a free action. While rooted, your body becomes an awakened locus: you gain \+1 Armor and \+1 Ward, perceive hidden dream-structures and ley-patterns, and can interface with the region’s dream-code. While in this state you may, as free actions:
>
> * Mind-Surf — You and up to (Level) nearby allies transmit your spiritual bodies through a nearby node or spirit glyph to another connected node within the Nexus (destination set by Referee or via a successful Arcane Alignment check). Your physical bodies remain at the locus.
> * Backrooms Access — You and up to (Level) nearby allies teleport physically up to (Level \+ Charisma) × 20 yd to a location your locus-sense can validly trace. Using Backroom Access ends the Dream state.
>
> End Conditions: The Dream state ends early if you move your physical body more than 5 yd, if you use Backroom Access (unless x4 overcharged as above), or if you make a Defeat roll.
>
> _Overcharge:_ *x2* — ally limit becomes (Level \+ Thought); Backroom Access distance becomes (Level \+ Charisma) × 40 yd. *x4* — you may use Backroom Access once without ending the Dream state; Mind-Surf can jump through two connected nodes in a chain.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:fantascience]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [anchored]
>   [concentration]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Avatar of the Dream; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

## Battle Shell

> **Battle Shell**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 1\. **R:** Self; aura 2 yd for ally cover.  
> **T:** Self (stance) and adjacent allies. **D:** While braced and until you move willingly.
>
> Requires a braced posture.
>
> Enter a braced stance; gain \+2 Defense, and ignore “shove/knock prone” effects that don’t also deal damage. Adjacent allies gain \+1 Defense while you remain braced. Enemies treat your zone as difficult terrain unless they beat a Strength test. Your shell becomes a temporary strongpoint — a caravan might even pitch a tent against you and feel safe.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — \+3 Defense while braced; x4 — adjacent allies also gain \+1 Defense.

## Breaker of Waves

> **Breaker of Waves**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 1\. **R:** (Level \+ Charisma) × 10 yd aura centered on you.  
> **T:** You and allies in aura. **D:** One crossing of the specified hazard (or 10 minutes, whichever is shorter).
>
> Effect: Once per watch, ignore difficult water, surf, sludge, or slick ice and grant Advantage on one roll to cross the same obstacle (including with mounts/vehicles).
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — ignore difficult terrain from rain, sleet, or grease-like effects; x4 — vehicles and mounts also gain \+2 to relevant control checks.

## Burrower’s Instinct

> **Burrower’s Instinct**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 1 **R:** 30 × 30 yd patch of natural ground (or native stone).  
> **T:** The surveyed area; self for the skill bonus. **D:** Mapping is instantaneous; the Recon bonus lasts one watch.
>
> Spend 1 power to nose-map the ground, detecting void pockets, newly-dug passages, and pressure-weak zones. You also gain Advantage on Recon checks about stonework, cave-ins, or tunnel stability for one watch.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — double the mapped footprint; x4 — also detect thin void membranes and dormant sinkholes.

## Call of the Deep

> **Call of the Deep**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** Self  
> **T:** Self **D:** One watch
>
> Your body flows into an aquatic form (tail, gills). You gain water breathing and Swim speed ×2 your normal Speed. Land movement is halved while in Sea-Form. Price: 3 Life (Affinity may reduce by 1, minimum 1).
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — gain \+1 Armor and Advantage on Swim checks for the duration; x4 — also gain passive water-sense within 10 yd (detects currents/large moving creatures).

## Crown of the Grave

> **Crown of the Grave**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** (Level \+ Thought) × 10 yd.  
> **T:** Each undead in range (choose individually). **D:** One watch.
>
> Declare your claim over nearby undead. Each target chooses:
>  • Accept — You and that undead gain \+1 to all rolls involving each other for the duration; you may share Power freely while within sight.
>  • Refuse — Target makes an Attrition (Wear & Tear) Save. On a fail, they lose 1 Endurance or Aura; if they cannot, they suffer Wear & Tear instead (max Life reduced by Level, fill 1 Burden slot until removed). Price: 2 Life (modified by Affinity).
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — add “Disoriented” to Refusers for 1 round on a failed save; x4 — you also gain passive sense of each affected target’s location in range.

## Dream-Skim

> **Dream-Skim**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** self  
> **T:** self (plus aura 10 yd for detection) **D:** 1 minute (concentration)
>
> You flutter at the edges of waking, dipping into the shared dream-stream that seeps through all nearby minds. For one minute you sense the presence of conscious or dreaming creatures within the aura, even through walls or darkness, though not their exact form or identity. With focus, you may glean a surface impression — fear, hunger, rage, or serenity — though strong wards or iron taboos may block this. At higher overcharge you can pierce deeper: ×2 expands your net wider, while ×4 pulls you into a target’s dreamscape, exposing you to both truths and nightmares until the scene ends.
>
> _Overcharge:_ ×2 — extend aura to 30 yd; ×4 — enter shared dream of one target in range for one scene.

>   [power]
>   [type:fantascience]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [concentration]
>   [dream]
>   [shadow]
>   [psychic]
>   [scout]

>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft

## Earthshaker

> **Earthshaker**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** self  
> **T:** self **D:** instant
>
> Stomp or strike the ground with force:
>
> * All creatures within 10 yards must Save (Endurance):
>   * **Fail**: knocked prone and take 1d6 damage.
>   * **Success**: momentarily staggered—treat as Disoriented for 1 round (−1 to all rolls).
> * If underground or in a structurally unstable area, roll 1d6: on a 1, a hazard or collapse is triggered (Referee decides).
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — standard escalation per referee call.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:other]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [earth]
>   [totem]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Earthshaker; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

## Echolocation Pulse

> **Echolocation Pulse**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 2 **R:** here (aura 20 yd)  
> **T:** zone (all within aura) **D:** 1 round
>
> Heritages: Bat Folk
>
>
>
> You let loose a rapid series of squeaks and trills, painting the world in echoes. For one round you gain blindsight within the aura, automatically perceiving hidden or invisible creatures, concealed doors, or traps that rely on moving parts. Foes hiding or cloaked in the zone must roll a save (Agility vs. your Thought) or be revealed to all allies for that round. The pulse does not carry through silence fields or heavy sound-dampening wards, and it may alert nearby creatures attuned to vibration.
>
> _Overcharge:_ ×2 — extend aura to 40 yd; ×4 — pierce solid barriers up to 5 yd thick.

>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>

> **T:** Self. **D:** Instantaneous (when reduced to 0 Life).
>
>  Effect: When you hit 0 Life, immediately cast one Power you know. If you have no Life to spend, pay its price in Ability score points instead (1 point \= 1 Life). If you cannot pay the full cost, the Power fails. Referee may call for a danger roll if applicable.
>

>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** self  
> **T:** self **D:** instant
>

>

> * Fail: flee or fall prone (referee chooses).
>
> If at least one enemy fails this Save, and you are a Player Daemon with a Hero Die pool, gain \+1 Hero Die. (If used by a non-Daemon NPC, treat the Hero Die as a 1-use bonus die usable within the scene.)

## Mist-Woven Hide

> **Mist-Woven Hide**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** Self  
> **T:** Self **D:** Up to 10 minutes, or until you end it (free action)
>
> Once per watch you may dissolve into swirling fog, becoming a semi-intangible mist (as Amorphous Body). You occupy your space, carry worn/held gear, and move normally, but you can’t perform fine manipulation or speak clearly. You can slip through narrow openings and cannot be pinned by effects that require firm purchase. Area effects and magic affect you normally. You lightly obscure your own space; gain Advantage on Stealth in dim light, smoke, or natural mist.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — While misted, gain \+2 Defense and Advantage on saves vs. grapple/restraints; you can seep through gaps ≥ 4 in/10 cm; x4 — You can seep through hairline cracks; you’re immune to grapple/shove, and nonmagical weapon attacks deal half damage to you.

## Myrmidon Surge

> **Myrmidon Surge**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 2 **R:** nearby (aura 10 yd)  
> **T:** each willing ally in aura (see modes **D:** 1 round
>
> Heritages: Ant Folk,
>
>
>
> You snap a drilled call/beat/volley that pulls bodies into one mind. Choose one mode when you cast:
>
> * **Onslaught:** Allies in the aura gain **\+2 to their first attack roll** this round. Once this round, if **two or more attached Units** in the aura have hits on the same target, you may resolve their damage as a **single Focused source** (Volley-style) **without spending a Command Die**.
> * **Phalanx:** Allies in the aura gain **\+2 Defense** until the start of your next turn. Once this round, **one attached Unit** in the aura may **Brace without being marked** (no tempo debt).
>
> The signal’s style varies by culture (shield-clash, chant, pheromone click), but the effect is the same: lanes open, shields lock, and the line moves as one.
>
> _Overcharge:_ ×2 — aura 20 yd; ×4 — apply both modes below instead of choosing one.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:fantascience]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [command]
>   [tactics]
>   [rite]
>   [network]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Myrmidon Surge; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

## Overmind Link

> **Overmind Link**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 8 (networked action economy \+ remote casting is potent). **R:** 1 mile.  
> **T:** You and up to (Level) allied constructs (including Vome). **D:** One watch; ends early if you voluntarily sever the link.
>
> Heritages: Awakened Vome
>
>  Effect: Merge thoughts; all linked share sensory input and mental Ability scores. Any Power you cast may originate from any linked body in the mesh. Price: 3 Life to initiate (modified by Affinity), then 1 Life per watch to maintain.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — also link 1 non-construct ally per 2 Levels; x4 — range becomes 5 miles along active DreamNet paths.

>   [power]

## Pheromone Beacon

> **Pheromone Beacon**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 1 **R:** here (trail along your path; aura 20 yd to read it)  
> **T:** this zone (allies within aura) **D:** scene (or until washed away)
>
> Heritages: Ant Folk
>
>
> You exude an invisible scent-code that binds to air currents and surfaces, leaving a persistent trail allies can sense within the aura. For the duration, allies who can read your pheromones gain advantage on checks to **track, regroup, or navigate back** along your route and cannot become **lost** by normal means in that zone. Hostiles can’t perceive the code unless they possess a comparable pheromone sense or relevant power. Heavy rain, strong solvents, or a silence-like field for scent will break the trail early.
>
> _Overcharge:_ ×2 — aura 40 yd and lasts one watch; ×4 — also spoofs a false trail that imposes disadvantage on enemy tracking for one scene.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:other]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [network]
>   [scent]
>   [scout]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft

## Shell Craft

> **Shell Craft**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 1 (baseline refit); complex refits see Overcharge. **R:** Self; touch items.  
> **T:** Your shell and attached gear/foci/harnesses. **D:** Until removed or damaged.
>
> Fueled by time, tools, and materials: 1 power per hour of work per Stone of gear integrated.
>
> Affix gear, ritual foci, shields, or quick-deploy harnesses directly to your shell; redesign and reinforce your retrofits as needed. Treat attached items as ready to draw/activate; referee may grant Advantage on “draw/brace” style actions that leverage the mounting.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — complete a complex retrofit in 10 minutes instead of 1 hour; x4 — add a “shell Inventory” to the character with one gear slot per hour spent (Skilled limit 3, Expert Limit 6, Master limit 9).

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:oldtech]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [fueled]

## Soul Anchor

> **Soul Anchor**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 8 (strong persistence effect). **R:** Touch (to bind); re-form occurs at the anchor.  
> **T:** A fixed object, site, or relic. **D:** Permanent until destroyed or ritually unbound.
>
> Fixed Object, Site, or Relic: locks 4 Life essence into the anchor. Your essence remains locked until you voluntarily unbind (1 hour) or the anchor is destroyed.
>
> Bind your spirit to the anchor. You cannot be permanently destroyed unless the anchor is destroyed. When reduced to 0 Life reform at the anchor after 1d6 minutes with half maximum Life. Use this 1/day, or recharge by spending a Hero Die.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — anchor can be moved with a 1-hour rite; x4 — when reforming, also clear 1 Burden.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:other]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [necromancy]
>   [anchor]
>   [persistence]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Soul Anchor; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

## Summon Guardian Spirit

> **Summon Guardian Spirit**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 6 **R:** self  
> **T:** self **D:** instant
>
> Once per session, call forth a guardian of bark and basalt from a shrine, ley-node, or elemental vein. The area becomes “Awakened” in the DreamNet.
>
> * Guardian Spirit: Level 3, Life 16, \+5 to actions, 1d6+3 damage, \+3 Armor/+3 Ward.
> * Duration: 1 watch (4 hours) or until defeated. When the spirit binding ends, make a Danger Roll vs Power spent.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — standard escalation per referee call.

  </div>

</div>

<div class="power-card" markdown="1">

## Surge

> **Surge**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** 15-yd cone  
> **T:** Creatures in cone **D:** Instantaneous, with knockback resolution
>
> Unleash a crashing wave. Creatures in the cone take 2d6\* damage and must Save (Endurance) or be knocked prone and pushed 1d6\* yd away from you. On a successful Save, they take half damage and are not pushed or knocked prone. Price: 3 Life (Affinity may reduce by 1, minimum 1).
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — deal \+1d6\* damage and push an additional 1d6\* yd; x4 — cone extends to 25 yd and targets make their save at Disadvantage.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:other]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [water]
>   [attack]
>   [control]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Surge; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

## Thunder Step

> **Thunder Step**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 2 **R:** self  
> **T:** self **D:** instant
>
> Dash 20 yd without provoking reactions and crackle with harmless lightning for one round.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — standard escalation per referee call.

## Venom Bolt

> **Venom Bolt**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 4 **R:** short  
> **T:** self **D:** instant
>
> The mage summons the overflowing love for all things into their Heart Chakra (green, center of chest), then cruelly inverts it and casts it towards their community's enemy. On a successful Charisma attack deal 1d6 life Damage and 1 point of Endurance damage. If they take any damage the target must make an Endurance save. On a failed save they take 1 point of life damage (venom) at the end of their turn for the next 1d6 rounds.
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — standard escalation per referee call.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:ritual]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [venom]
>   [gaze]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Venom Bolt; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.

<div class="power-card" markdown="1">

## Warren-Soul

> **Warren-Soul**
>
> _FTLS power invocation_
>
> **P:** 2 **R:** 1 zone you can reasonably enclose/define as “warren” (camp, cave, ship compartment).  
> **T:** The chosen place; allies within. **D:** Until dawn or until you leave the area for a full watch.
>
> Once per day, declare a “home warren.” Allies inside gain \+1 to saves vs fear and environmental hazards. You always know the shortest path back to the warren and can squeeze your body through any passage that a Small creature could manage (you contort like a seasoned burrower).
>
> _Overcharge:_ x2 — also grants \+1 Defense inside; x4 — you may designate two small connected zones as one warren.

tags:
>   [power]
>   [type:ritual]
>   [storage:trait]
>   [earth]
>   [ward]
>   [rite]

meta:
> - source:
>   - book: Flying_Triremes_and_Laser_Swords_06_Powers; page: working-draft
> - usage:
>   - scope: power; id: Warren-Soul; note: FTLS Chapter 06 alpha power entry.
